contested","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-outlook-how-invest-election-uncertain-advice-contested-stovall-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9845810c60aa00190d4858?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump biden\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Business Insider spoke with Sam Stovall, CFRA chief investment strategist, on how to invest during an unpredictable US election season.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>Stovall cautioned investors against trying to \"guess\" who will win the election, especially given how incorrect the polls were in 2016.</strong></li><li><strong>The chief strategist also said investors could use a contested election and subsequent pullback as a time to buy stocks at a discount.</strong></li></ul><ul><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestutm_source=msn.com&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=msn-slideshow&utm_campaign=bodyurl?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestsource=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\"><strong>Visit the Business Insider homepage for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>The upcoming US election is leaving many investors uncertain about how to manage their portfolios. While national polls point to a clear Joe Biden win, many investors are looking back at 2016 and skeptical of polling. In addition, the surge of mail-in voting has increased the likelihood that the outcome of the election may be unknown for a while after November 3.</p><p>Business Insider spoke with Sam Stovall, CFRA chief investment strategist, to discuss how investors should position their portfolios during this unpredictable election season.&#160;</p><p>Stovall cautioned investors against trying to \"guess\" who will win the election and making investment decisions based on that projection.</p><p>\"You're taking a big gamble being wrongly positioned should 2020 end up looking like 2016, in which the polls were wrong,\" the investment strategist said.&#160;</p><p>Instead, investors should stick with their strategy no matter who they think will win, or who actually ends up winning. CFRA is neutral on both stocks and bonds.</p><p>\"If you have a strategy, then stick to that strategy no matter who ends up becoming president or whom you think will become president,\" Stovall said. \"If you're a momentum player, stick with momentum.\"</p><p>The coronavirus has also complicated prediction models that typically provide investors with a clearer idea of who will win. Stovall referenced the Presidential Predictor model, which tracks the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500_500\">S&#38;P 500</a> price change from July 31 to October 31 before the election. Since 1944, the model has shown that if the price change was positive, the incumbent political party will remain in office.</p><p>This model has failed only twice, during years when the US faced what Stovall calls \"geopolitical disruptors\" — the Vietnam War and the Iranian Hostage crisis. He said coronavirus could be the 2020 \"disruptor\" that explains why Trump may not win reelection, even if the S&#38;P 500 price change is positive heading into the election.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-invest-in-bull-market-volatility-elections-morgan-stanley-2020-10\" data-analytics-position=\"4\" data-analytics-module=\"\">MORGAN STANLEY: Stocks could fall another 9% as the new bull market faces a rising tide of risks — and these 2 cyclical sectors are the best long-term trades to take advantage of</a></em></p><p>If the election is contested and the outcome is uncertain for a few weeks, Stovall expects there to be a pullback in stocks. In 2000, the market fell 10% as it awaited the election decision, he said.</p><p>However, this pullback could provide an opportunity to buy at a discount stocks that have heated up recently, like alternative fuels and cannabis.</p><p>\"Look for those stocks that got away from you during the recent recouping of the prior bear market. And identify which ones you would like to own at lower prices,\" said the strategist. \"Then, once they hit your target price, act upon it because you're never really going to be able to capture the ultimate bottom.\"</p><p>Stovall also said an additional selloff is likely if Biden wins, as investors take some profits in anticipation of the former vice president's capital-gains tax hike.</p><p>Ultimately, investors should remember that the market is forward looking, and is more focused on economics than politics, he said.&#160;</p><p>Monday's stock selloff was likely due to the worry that the surge in coronavirus cases could lower fourth quarter gross domestic product and earnings, said Stovall. Thursday's reported third quarter GDP growth is estimated to be 31%, and the market may react negatively if the number is lower.</p><p>\"Because the estimate is so high, I actually think all things being equal, you have a greater chance of being disappointed than that you are being overly pleased,\" Stovall said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-outlook-how-invest-election-uncertain-advice-contested-stovall-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 27 Oct 2020 16:34:31 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f80c93fea74820019ca65c8?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"95e2f7fc06e96cf9a5ddd7475e4a6f56","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn88@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-54-10-965_85028f8bec20b0e4.webp","destWidth":2246,"destHeight":1684,"sourceBytes":144850,"destBytes":144850,"author":"egraffeo@businessinsider.com (Emily Graffeo)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f9845810c60aa00190d4858?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn53@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-04-777_651db421d45daf4c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626706},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"Federal judge rejects Justice Department's effort to defend Trump in E. Jean Carroll rape defamation suit","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/judge-rejects-dojs-effort-to-defend-trump-rape-defamation-suit-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9307ad212113001874077a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump wind\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A federal judge on Tuesday rejected an effort from the Justice Department to remove President Donald Trump as the defendant in a defamation case.&#160;</li>\n<li>Trump is being sued for defamation by writer E. Jean Carroll, who has accused the president of raping her in the 1990s.&#160;</li>\n<li>The president denied Carroll's allegations and said she was lying to boost sales of her book.&#160;</li>\n<li>\"His comments concerned an alleged sexual assault that took place several decades before he took office,\" US District Judge Lewis A. Kaplan said of Trump, adding that the \"allegations have no relationship to the official business of the United States.\"&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A federal judge on Tuesday squashed an effort by the Justice Department to remove President Donald Trump as the defendant in a defamation suit from a woman who's accused the commander-in-chief of rape.&#160;</p><p>The Justice Department requested that the United States government replace Trump as the defendant in the lawsuit, in which the president is accused of defaming writer E. Jean Carroll.&#160;</p><p>Caroll has accused Trump of raping her in a department store dressing room in the 1990s, which the president has vehemently denied. After Caroll came forward with the allegation, Trump accused her of lying and said she was trying to \"sell a book.\" The president denied ever meeting Carroll, though there's a 1987 photo of the two together.</p><p>The Justice Department contended that Trump was acting as a government employee with regard to his comments on Carroll, attempting to establish this as the basis for removing the president as the defendant in the lawsuit.&#160;</p><p>US District Judge Lewis A. Kaplan rejected the Justice Department's argument.&#160;</p><p>\"The President of the United States is not an employee of the Government within the meaning of the relevant statutes,\" Kaplan wrote. \"Even if he were such an employee, President Trumps allegedly defamatory statements concerning Ms. Carroll would not have been within the scope of his employment. Accordingly, the motion to substitute the United States in place of President Trump is denied.\"</p><p>\"His comments concerned an alleged sexual assault that took place several decades before he took office,\" the judge said of Trump, adding that the \"allegations have no relationship to the official business of the United States.\"&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f983d190c60aa00190d4803?format=jpeg\" alt=\"E. Jean Carroll\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>E. Jean Carroll at her home in Warwick, NY in 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/jean-carroll-at-her-home-in-warwick-ny-carroll-claims-that-news-photo/1180045462?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Eva Deitch for The Washington Post/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Kaplan's ruling essentially means that Trump can be sued personally over the matter. If the Justice Department had been successful in their effort to remove Trump as the defendant and replace him with the US government, it's likely the case would've been dismissed due to the legal doctrine of sovereign immunity, which bars private citizens from suing the federal government without its consent.</p><p>It's unclear whether the Justice Department will appeal the ruling, and a spokesperson did not immediately respond to Insider's request for comment.&#160;</p><p>Carroll's lawyer celebrated Tuesday's ruling, which came just one week before Election Day.&#160;</p><p>\"The simple truth is that President Trump defamed our client because she was brave enough to reveal that he had sexually assaulted her, and that brutal, personal attack cannot be attributed to the Office of the President,\" attorney Roberta Kaplan said in a statement provided to Insider. \"Judge Kaplan's words speak for themselves.\"&#160;</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe\n Insider</a></div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 27 Oct 2020 15:41:30 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f92c565abcd0c0018d69486?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"d38a1127fb91df92f812432071e5f0b8","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn60@2020_6/2020/10/27/16-54-01-313_dd09f8931ad13e34.webp","destWidth":2222,"destHeight":1666,"sourceBytes":83484,"destBytes":83484,"author":"insider@insider.com (John Haltiwanger)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f9307ad212113001874077a?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn23@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-54-03-232_689c1c7d6331cabd.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f983d190c60aa00190d4803?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn74@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-54-10-012_b3d973a23d197c4c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626751},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"I'm a freelance travel journalist. Here's how I take time off — even during a pandemic — without falling behind or losing crucial business.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-a-freelance-journalist-takes-vacation-without-losing-business-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f32d3164dca68415d3618ae?format=jpeg\" alt=\"digital nomad\" height=\"800\" width=\"1067\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You may craft more lucrative ideas while you&#39;re refreshing.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/search/photographer?family=creative&#38;photographer=Cavan&#43;Images\" target=\"_blank\">Cavan Images/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Lola M&#233;ndez is a freelance travel journalist.</li>\n<li>Two years ago, she took her first real vacation in years &#8212; and was miserable.</li>\n<li>She was operating in a scarcity mindset, fixated on all of the opportunities she might be missing.</li>\n<li>Here's how she's learned to take restful vacations, and shifted towards an abundance mentality.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Salaried workers have it good in many ways.&#160;</p><p>Their benefits often include partially-funded healthcare coverage, 401K matching programs, paid sick days, and even paid time off for bank holidays and vacation. Many people even negotiate their vacation days before accepting an offer for a new role.&#160;</p><p>Freelancers get none of these perks. Sure, we get to set our own rates and choose clients that align with our passions and expertise. But when it comes to getting away from it all and going off the grid for a few days, freelancers often struggle to mitigate stress. After all, a day away from work is a day bringing in zero earnings for freelancers who don't have passive income.</p><p>I'm all too familiar with the struggle of vacationing as a freelancer — especially as an independent travel journalist. It's nearly impossible for me to switch out of work mode when vacationing. I'm constantly searching for story angles, scribbling notes, chatting with locals, and snapping photos. Even when I'm not traveling on assignment, I act as if I am.</p><p>Two years ago I booked a week-long getaway on a Cambodian island with very little internet access. It was my first real vacation in years. I had zero obligation to write about the place where I was going. I expected to spend all day sunbathing at the beach, reading in a hammock swaying underneath palm trees, and enjoying all the cocktails my heart desired. Leading up to my trip I got all my assignments turned in on time and alerted my editors that I'd be offline.</p><h2>I was miserable in paradise.&#160;</h2><p>After a few hours of truly relaxing, I'd want to work. I love my job and the travel-centric lifestyle I've created for myself. Forcing myself to take a vacation didn't serve me. I was desperate to check my emails. I couldn't wait to return to the mainland and get back online. I was operating on the scarcity mindset and was afraid of all the opportunities I was missing by being offline.</p><p>I've since learned how to embrace a short holiday. Spending three to five days offline is my sweet spot. I can truly enjoy my experience without worrying too much about work. Even though I'm typically overseas, I tend to schedule my vacations around US bank holidays, since that's when most of my clients will also be offline. I know it's unlikely I'll have unexpected edits or assignments due over a long holiday weekend.</p><h2>To be able to enjoy your vacation, notify your clients as soon as possible about the dates you're taking off work and assure them you'll meet all deadlines before you jet off.&#160;</h2><p>As a journalist, I usually have a handle full of articles in various stages of editing. I email any and all editors who may email me with edits while I'm gone to let them know I'll be OOO.</p><p>If you get incoming work close to your scheduled vacation, be realistic with yourself about whether you can fulfill the duties before your holiday. I try not to accept new deadlines two weeks before my departure. Ask your clients if they have any wiggle room with the deadline and try to schedule it for a week after you return from vacation.&#160;</p><p>Don't take on too much extra work to make up for the \"lost time,\" or you'll be so burnt out on your vacation that you won't be able to enjoy your time off.&#160;</p><p>If your clients give you grief about taking off, it might be time to consider if you want to end your professional relationship with them. Freedom is one of the key reasons many take a freelance career path. Do you want to work with someone who makes you feel guilty about cultivating a healthy work-life balance?</p><p>I don't work for an intelligence agency. My work will not save the world from imploding. It can wait until I'm back. I try to truly log off during my vacations and not check my email. If I'm going away for a long weekend from Thursday to Monday I usually don't take my laptop with me.&#160;</p><h2>I always put up a vacation responder on my email.&#160;</h2><p>In the subject, I include what day I'll be back online. My biggest tip is to write that you'll be online a day after you're actually back in the office. That way you have a day to clean up your inbox (which will inevitably be filled with emails).</p><p>In my out of office message, I state if I'll have internet access and when folks can expect a response back from me. If I'll have access to email, I'll note that I'm checking emails once a day and that if the request is truly urgent to email me back with URGENT in the subject line so I know which emails need a quick response before I'm back on the clock.</p><p>If, like me, you have daily clients, try not to get too caught up in thinking about the money you're \"missing out on\" by taking a few days off. I know this is difficult. One of my gigs is as a trending news writer. Most days I earn between $120-$290. A week away from this work means I could lose up to $1,450.&#160;</p><p>But, when I come back from my holiday, I usually have crystalized a few ideas for features that could earn me double that amount. You'll be able to make up that lost income when you return from your holiday refreshed, and ready to jump back into work with a renewed energy.&#160;</p><h2>Your clients aren't going to forget you because you took a vacation.&#160;</h2><p>They'll benefit from the improvement in your work after you've rested. Your business will continue to thrive, and may even blossom after you unwind on vacation.</p><p>Adopting the abundance mentality has been tremendous in helping me feel confident that spending a few days away from my inbox won't be detrimental to my career. Yes, freelancers have zero job security, but I remain positive that money is always coming my way. There will always be more opportunities. Freelancing ebbs and flows — there are great months and awful months whether or not you're glued to your computer screen or spending a few days getting lost in the woods.</p><p><em>This Business Insider article was originally published on October 24, 2020.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a throwing away \"approximately\" 111 absentee ballots along with other mail in a construction dumpster.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.justice.gov/usao-wdky/pr/feds-charge-postal-employee-destroying-mail\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"eee94fe4a50f5fc60fa199f78fe3d506\">US Department of Justice</a> on Monday said DeShawn Bojgere, 30, of Louisville, had been charged with the delay or destruction of mail after telling federal authorities he was responsible for discarding the mail. If convicted, Bojgere faces a maximum penalty of five years in prison and a fine of $250,000.</p><p>A criminal complaint accuses Bojgere of dumping a \"large quantity\" of mail sometime between October 5 and October 15. The mail was discovered in a construction dumpster in Louisville. In addition to more than 100 absentee ballots that had been sent from the Jefferson County Clerk's Office to voters to fill out, the discarded mail also contained about 70 pieces of flat-rate mail, 320 pieces of second-class mail, and \"two national election campaign flyers from a political party in Florida,\" according to US Attorney Russell Coleman's office.&#160;</p><p>The discarded mail had been from a single day and the same route, the Justice Department said. Copies of the mail were made for evidence in the case, but the original copies were eventually sent back into delivery, the Justice Department said.</p><p>\"Especially in these times, Americans depend on the reliability and integrity of those that deliver the US Mail,\" Coleman said in a press release. \"Conduct by Postal employees that violates that duty will result in swift federal prosecution.\"</p><p>Despite <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-states-require-to-verify-absentee-ballots-prevent-fraud-map-2020-10\">evidence mail-in voting is largely safe and secure</a>, President Donald Trump has for months <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-mail-in-voting-claims-republicans-warn-could-cost-election-2020-9\">launched attacks on the Postal Service</a> and states' efforts to encourage voters to cast ballots by mail during the coronavirus pandemic.</p><p>On Monday, the president once again attacked mail-in voting, claiming in a tweet — href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/twitter-trump-tweet-mail-voting-warning-label-minsinformation-block-retweet-2020-10\">Twitter labeled the tweet as potentially misleading and stopped other users 2020 16:11:48 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"Fauci: 5 science-backed reasons you should keep your mask on at all times during the pandemic — even when visiting friends","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-5-reasons-to-wear-a-mask-during-the-pandemic-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c13c07f9786001d1f89b8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"fauci vaccine\" height=\"3300\" width=\"2200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dr. Anthony Fauci, director of the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases, on June 30, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Al Drago/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The White House says \"we are not going to control the pandemic.\"</li>\n<li>But Dr. Anthony Fauci disagrees, and scientific evidence is on his side.</li>\n<li>Fauci and two of his colleagues from the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Disease co-authored a new JAMA viewpoint.</li>\n<li>They lay out why a combination of \"low-tech\" coronavirus-fighting measures, including masks, distancing, handwashing, and fast testing are all critical for controlling the pandemic.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The White House is calling it quits on fighting the coronavirus.&#160;</p><p>\"We are not going to control the pandemic,\" President Trump's chief of staff, Mark Meadows, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mark-meadows-donald-trump-white-house-coronavirus-treatment-vaccine-2020-10\">told CNN on Sunday</a>.&#160;</p><p>But America's top infectious disease expert is still in it to win it.&#160;</p><p>Dr. Anthony Fauci says one of the most potent and \"low-tech\" things everyone can do right now to help control the spread of this virus is also extremely simple: keep on wearing that mask.</p><p>Fauci stressed the disease-fighting measure once again Monday in a Journal of the American Medical Association (JAMA) viewpoint, authored with his colleagues Dr. Andrea Lerner and Dr. Gregory Folkers from the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases.</p><p>The trio's science-backed mask up reminder comes just as the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-third-coronavirus-case-surge-outbreak-deadliest-largest-yet-2020-10\">US is dealing with its greatest surge of coronavirus</a> infections yet, and with a decent, widely-available coronavirus vaccine still many months away.&#160;</p><p>\"Ultimately, a safe and effective vaccine will be essential to control the pandemic and allow resumption of the many activities of normal life,\" Fauci and his colleagues wrote <a href=\"https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jama/fullarticle/2772459\">in their JAMA letter</a>.&#160;</p><p>But, in the meantime, we have a few \"low-tech\" tools which are going to be essential to controlling the spread of this new virus, the doctors said. And masks are a major one.&#160;</p><p>The others we already have include: \"physical distancing, hand hygiene, prompt testing (along with isolation and contact tracing), and limits on crowds and gatherings,\" Fauci and his colleagues said.</p><p>None of these interventions, taken on its own, will fully end the pandemic, but together they can work to dramatically cut down on the number of coronavirus infections and deaths we will see in the weeks and months ahead.</p><p>\"Return to normalcy,\" Fauci and his colleagues said, \"will require the widespread acceptance and adoption of mask wearing and other inexpensive and effective interventions.\"</p><p>Here are the biggest reasons why Fauci and his colleagues are arguing it's really important to for everyone keep on donning a mask during the pandemic:&#160;</p><h2>Mask usage goes hand in hand with lower COVID-19 infection rates in the US, and around the world&#160;</h2><p>There is a clear pattern that has been established at this point in the pandemic, based on studies conducted in hospitals and homes around the world: wherever masks are worn, coronavirus transmission rates tumble.</p><p>A <a href=\"https://gh.bmj.com/content/5/5/e002794.full\">study of 124 households in Beijing</a> conducted early-on in the pandemic, which Fauci and his co-authors cited, found that Chinese families who wore masks at home before anyone in the house ever knew they were sick with the virus saw lower odds of secondary infections (face mask use was \"79% effective in reducing transmission,\" the study said.)&#160;</p><p>And, <a href=\"http://jamanetwork.com/article.aspx?doi=10.1001/jama.2020.12897\">in Massachussetts' largest hospital system</a>, after all health care workers and patients started wearing masks, virus \"positivity rate among health care workers declined from 14.65% to 11.46%, with a decline of 0.49% per day,\" Fauci's viewpoint said.&#160;</p><p>Modeling studies back up this same idea on population-wide level, suggesting that putting on a face covering not only prevents more disease, it also saves lives.&#160;</p><p>Mask mandates may have \"averted <a href=\"https://www.healthaffairs.org/doi/10.1377/hlthaff.2020.00818\">more than 200,000 cases</a> of COVID-19 [the disease caused by the coronavirus] by May 22, 2020,\" according to another study Fauci that and his co-authors cited.&#160;</p><p>More recent modeling estimates likewise suggest that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/universal-masks-save-lives-mitigate-third-surge-model-2020-10\">if every American put on a mask now, more than 130,000 more US deaths</a> could be prevented, by March 2021.&#160;</p><p>\"Expanding mask use can be one of the 'easy wins' in the United States,\" Christopher Murray, director of the University of Washington's Institute for Health Metrics and Evaluation (IHME), told reporters on Friday, as that new model was released.</p><h2>Masks also keep other people's germs closer to them</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ef645995af6cc10aa64b6d2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"coronavirus task force fauci \" height=\"1467\" width=\"2200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Director of the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases Dr. Anthony Fauci watches as Vice President Mike Pence speaks after leading a White House Coronavirus Task Force briefing at the Department of Health and Human Services on June 26, 2020 in Washington, DC.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joshua Roberts/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Masks are the kind of armor you want everyone to wear.&#160;</p><p>They keep infected people's germs closer to them, and as such are \"a logical strategy to curb transmission,\" Fauci and his colleagues said.</p><p>Even when people aren't <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-coronavirus-can-travel-6-feet-through-the-air-indoors-2020-10\">shouting, laughing, or singing</a> (activities we know can spread the virus well) \"masks can reduce respiratory virus shedding in exhaled breath,\" which means not only are other people less likely to get sick from being around infected individuals wearing masks, they may, possibly, also get a milder case of the coronavirus, if indeed they do become infected.&#160;</p><h2>Keep your mask on, even when you're talking</h2><p>Indoors, in stuffy, stagnant spaces without good ventilation, coronavirus particles can more easily linger in the air.&#160;</p><p>That's why you should try to keep your mask on as much as possible.</p><p>\"With the onset of colder weather in the northern hemisphere, activities will increasingly occur inside, resulting in often-unavoidable congregating,\" Fauci and his colleagues said.&#160;</p><p>Knowing that such crowded, indoor spaces can be prone to a buildup of more virus in the air, \"the commonly observed practice of individuals removing their mask when speaking is not advisable,\" Fauci said.&#160;</p><h2>Some people might never realize they have COVID-19, so everyone should wear a mask as much as possible</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f21a0c55af6cc2610358444?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Fauci Baseball\" height=\"683\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rob Carr/Staff/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Another reason to wear a mask? Asymptomatic virus spread.</p><p>\"Recent evidence suggests that up to 40% to 45% of people infected with [the coronavirus] may never be symptomatic, but still can transmit the virus,\" Fauci and his colleagues said.&#160;</p><p>Because this means we can never, really, know exactly who has the virus and who doesn't, \"universal mask wearing in the community for source control is recommended,\" they added.&#160;</p><h2>Testing alone doesn't work</h2><p>This strategy was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/when-to-get-tested-for-covid-quarantine-2020-10\">tried, and failed, at the White House</a> already.</p><p>\"No test is perfect,\" Fauci and his colleagues said.&#160;</p><p>Tests can produce false negative results (telling people they're sick when they're really not), and all tests \"have a lower limit of detection,\" the doctors said, which means some cases of the coronavirus may never get picked up by a test.&#160;</p><p>\"In addition, the result of a test represents just one point in time and does not indicate an individual's status outside of the moment the specimen was collected,\" Fauci and his co-authors added.</p><p>This is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dont-rely-on-rapid-covid-19-tests-party-see-parents-2020-8\">another way to say that a negative test one day</a> won't, necessarily, mean you'll test negative for the virus the next, or the next.&#160;</p><p>\"Reliance on testing alone to prevent transmission will be ineffective without the use of additional strategies such as mask wearing and physical distancing,\" Fauci and his colleagues said.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Ted Cruz says the mounting national debt will re-emerge as a major concern for the GOP.</li>\n<li>The deficit had been growing even before the pandemic hammered the American economy as a result of the 2017 tax cuts and spending increases that Trump had enacted with GOP backing.</li>\n<li>Many Republicans are reluctant to support another pandemic aid bill, citing the growing federal debt.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Sen. Ted Cruz said the growing national debt is set to broadly re-emerge as an area of concern of Republicans down the road.</p><p>During an interview on \"Axios on HBO\" with political reporter Jonathan Swan, the Texas Republican discussed the budget deficit and the federal debt. The pair had an energetic back-and-forth on the matter, with Swan saying Republicans had approved spending policies that grew the deficit, like the 2017 tax cuts.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ted-cruz-trump-federal-debt-eliminate-2016-campaign-national-deficit-2020-10\">Cruz also claimed Trump</a> never ran on cutting the debt, but the president campaigned in 2016 to eliminate it within eight years.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Axios  (@axios) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1320935753996787712?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 27, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Asked if the swelling debt and deficit will become an area of concern for the GOP, Cruz responded: \"Sure.\"</p><p>\"Isn't that the most cynical, phony thing?\" Swan asked.</p><p>\"You're touching into something that as you know I've raged against,\" Cruz replied. \"I've raged against my own party not genuinely fighting to rein in spending and deficits and debt.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong>&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-trade-election-democrat-focused-strategies-columbia-threadneedle-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"d69584d099472cf56801ef131767abf2\">An investing shop overseeing $476 billion analyzed 650 stocks to fine-tune its election strategy. The firm's experts break down the trades to make around a Biden win — and explains how investors can keep portfolios safe.</a></em></p><p>The Trump administration enacted a $1.9 trillion tax law in 2017 that mostly benefited large corporations with strong support from Republicans, <a href=\"https://www.c-span.org/video/?c4701424/user-clip-ted-cruz-defends-tax-cuts-jobs-act-home-schoolers\">including</a> Cruz. Congress and Trump <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/congress-spending-bills-4-big-policy-changes-passed-government-trump-2019-12-1028773121#\">also approved</a> significant spending increases in 2018.</p><p>As a result of the pandemic, the budget deficit — the gap between tax revenue and federal spending — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-federal-budget-deficit-record-trillion-coronavirus-stimulus-recession-2020-10\">grew to $3.1 trillion</a> for fiscal year 2020, three times the size it was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-deficit-fiscal-2019-hits-984-billion-3rd-straight-gain-2019-10\">last year</a>. The larger amount reflects the government action undertaken to confront the pandemic, but <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/charts-contrasting-trump-economy-obama-bush-administrations-republicans-democrats-2020-10\">the deficit had been growing</a> before 2019 as well.</p><p>The largest chunk of spending came from the $2 trillion economic aid package known as the CARES Act approved in late March, which contained $1,200 stimulus checks, $600 enhanced unemployment insurance, and small business aid, among other measures.</p><p>In recent months, many Republicans have opposed another federal rescue package, citing the growing federal debt. The White House and Democrats are discussing another stimulus bill that could be nearly $2 trillion with Trump's strong backing. Republican Sen. Rick Scott of Florida blasted the price tag under consideration on Tuesday.</p><p>\"We've got to understand that we've got to get our fiscal house in order,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SquawkCNBC/status/1321063797780549632?s=20\">Scott told CNBC</a>. \"Somebody is going to have to pay for this.\"</p><p>But Federal Reserve officials and budget experts across the political spectrum argue more spending is needed to prop up a weakening economy.</p><p>Permanent layoffs are mounting and millions of Americans are still out of work. Employees at the American company could face termination and salary cuts if they do not return to the office.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apparel-workers-forced-return-to-office-face-firing-pay-cuts-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">'We're terrified': The company that makes Calvin Klein and Guess jeans is forcing workers to head back into a full-capacity office or be fired</a></em></p><p>As more offices open up, Business Insider wants to hear how it's going. How did your company communicate the reopening process and the reason for returning? Are there consequences at your company for not returning to the office? <a href=\"https://forms.gle/8A1iuXWVsiMtbpfQ6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fill out this form</a> to share your experience and a reporter from Business Insider will reach out to hear more before anything is published.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/how-is-your-company-handling-the-return-to-the-office-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 27 Oct 2020 14:46:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f92cf67abcd0c0018d694a0?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"72ee29cd562ab7e31696d6f86f5d969f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn62@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-54-04-830_382d86adeb45739c.webp","destWidth":1365,"destHeight":1024,"sourceBytes":150854,"destBytes":150854,"author":"insider@insider.com (Shoshy Ciment)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f92cfb2212113001874060b?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn28@2020_1/2020/10/27/16-54-08-266_99a578120166b8c7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626686},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"How the secretive Special Boat Service — the UK's SEAL Team 6 — trains to recapture hijacked ships at sea","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-british-sbs-commandos-train-to-recapture-hijacked-ships-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96a0a44743a3001216b8b4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Nave Andromeda southampton hijacking\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Nave Andromeda docked at Southampton, October 26 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Henry Nicholls/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>On Sunday, British military operators from the secretive SBS swept aboard a hijacked ship in the English Channel, captured the suspected hijackers, and freed the crew &#8212; all in seven minutes.</li>\n<li>The efficiency and effectiveness the operation belies the complexities of maritime counterterrorism and the decades that the SBS has spent honing its craft.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>On Sunday night, British frogmen from the secretive Special Boat Service (SBS) <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uk-elite-sbs-raided-oil-tanker-suspected-hijacking-2020-10\" target=\"_top\">stormed a tanker</a> following a suspected hijacking by stowaways.</p><p>In just seven minutes, the SBS operators swept the gigantic ship, captured the suspected hijackers, and freed the crew. But the British commandos' efficiency and effectiveness belies the enormous complexities of maritime counterterrorism operations.</p><h2>Experts in retaking ships</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9835e00c60aa00190d47d6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"British SBS Special Boat Service\" height=\"400\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SBS operators in a rigid inflatable boat approaching a target.\n<p class=\"copyright\">British Ministry of Defense</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>This is the second such operation by SBS commandos in recent years. In December 2018, stowaways threatened the crew of a cargo ship in the Thames estuary, triggering a response by the SBS, who raided the ship and captured the men responsible.</p><p>Maritime counterterrorism is probably one of the toughest skill sets to learn. To begin with, it demands mastery of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/weapons-gear-used-by-us-military-special-operations-delta-seals-2020-10\" target=\"_top\">Close Quarters Battle (CQB)</a>, which takes years and thousands upon thousands of rounds to acquire.</p><p>As in all special-operations mission sets, top physical fitness is of the essence in maritime counterterrorism, particularly upper-body strength and endurance, as operators have to scale small ladders dangling treacherously between two moving vessels.</p><p>Add the unforgiving sea to the equation and you have a tough nut to crack.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9835e1861cb70019936a3f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"British SBS Special Boat Service\" height=\"1000\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Royal Marine Commandos during a Visit, Board, Search, and Seizure (VBSS) exercise.\n<p class=\"copyright\">British Ministry of Defense</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In an operation like the one on Nave Andromeda, the SBS would use multiple insertion methods to get on the ship. The aim is to divide the terrorists' or criminals' attention and disorient them by storming different parts of the vessel.</p><p>Usually, fast-moving boats would assault the target from both sides, and the operators in them would climb aboard the ship on ladders. At the same time, operators would fast-rope from hovering helicopters.</p><p>Once on board, the operators would simultaneously sweep the vessel from all angles (top, bottom, left, and right) to reach the hostages and neutralize the threat to them as soon as possible.</p><p>In addition, snipers would provide overwatch support and intelligence from helicopters flying above the target.</p><h2>Pioneers in maritime counterterrorism</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9835e10c60aa00190d47d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"British SBS Special Boat Service\" height=\"767\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SBS operators assaulting an oil rig during an exercise.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/jason_carl_fox/\" target=\"_blank\">Jason Fox/Instagram</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The SBS is the first special-operations unit in the world to adopt a maritime counterterrorism role. In May 1972, the Queen Elizabeth 2 cruise ship was sailing in the Atlantic Ocean when someone called the ship's company and threatened to blow it up unless a ransom was paid.</p><p>In response to the threat, four commandos, including two SBS operators, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/1972/05/19/archives/front-page-1-no-title-bombs-are-hunted-on-queen-elizabeth-2.html\" target=\"_top\">parachuted</a> into the ocean and boarded the ship.</p><p>In the end, the call was a hoax, but the incident showcased<!-- I took the reference to the Munich hostage crisis out because that wasn't a maritime incident, unless there was something about Munich specifically that led to SBS' expansion? --><!-- The Munich massacre was a milestone in counterterrorism and essentially created the skill set. Delta Force and SEAL Team 6 were created because of event, and the SAS and SBS began specializing in CT because of it, which necessitated a minor expansion.   --> the need for a dedicated maritime counterterrorism unit that could respond to future contingencies. The hostage crisis at the 1972 Munich Olympics underscored the importance of the counterterrorism mission.</p><p>As a result, the SBS began to grow, and the unit's counterterrorism mandate expanded to include anything maritime-related, such as cruise ships, channel ferries, or oil rigs. The SBS works closely with oil companies, often leasing active or decommissioned oil rigs so SBS troops can hone their skills.</p><p>The SBS' maritime counterterrorism skills are so good that when the North Sea oil industry began to swell in the 1970s and 1980s, many operators were lured away by oil companies' luxurious paychecks for security work, which caused a manning crisis in the elite unit at the time.</p><p>But the SBS has proven it can do more than maritime counterterrorism.</p><h2>By strength and guile</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9835e1861cb70019936a3e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"British SBS Special Boat Service\" height=\"596\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SBS and Delta Force operators during the Battle of Tora Bora.\n<p class=\"copyright\">CBS 60 Minutes/Defense Department</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Comprised of four assault squadrons (C, M, X, Z), the SBS specializes in direct action, special reconnaissance, counterterrorism, and hostage rescue. At any given time, a squadron is on standby to respond immediately to a terrorist attack or hostage situation in a maritime environment anywhere in the world.</p><p>Like the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/navy-seals-rusty-after-scandals-middle-east-wars-insiders-say-2020-10\" target=\"_top\">US Navy SEALs</a>, the last two decades of war in the Middle East have somewhat diverted the SBS from its maritime focus. But back-to-back deployments to Iraq and Afghanistan have shown the unit's land-warfare capabilities.</p><p>In the initial days of the campaign against Al Qaeda and the Taliban in Afghanistan, SBS operators fought alongside US Delta Force commandos in the Battle of Tora Bora, where Osama bin Laden was almost killed or captured in November 2001.</p><p>They also helped quell the Taliban prisoner riot that killed CIA operative Mike Spann, the first American to die in the Global War on Terror. During that operation, a US Navy SEAL from SEAL Team 6, who was serving on an exchange with the SBS, <a href=\"https://valor.militarytimes.com/hero/3630\" target=\"_top\">received the Navy Cross</a>, which is second only to the Medal of Honor.</p><p>Until recently, only Royal Marine Commandos could become SBS operators. Now all British service members, regardless of branch, can try out for the unit. They have to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-non-us-special-operations-forces-from-around-the-world-2020-8\" target=\"_top\">undergo a joint selection process with SAS candidates</a> and complete an additional months-long phase of maritime training at the end in order to qualify as SBS operators.</p><section data-track-content=\"\" data-post-type=\"post\"><p><em>Stavros Atlamazoglou is a defense journalist specializing in special operations, a Hellenic Army veteran (National Service with the 575th Marine Battalion &#38; Army HQ), and a Johns Hopkins University graduate.</em></p></section><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Whether you're interested in social justice reform, climate activism, or even just laying out arguments more efficiently, it helps to have a solid grasp of political science, history, and theory.&#160;</p><p>Of course, US politics is an incredibly broad topic, and it can be tough to know where to start. The online courses below provide in-depth lessons on a specific subject, from how the US government functions to the history of capitalism. Provided by schools like Harvard, Yale, Cornell, Georgetown, and the University of Michigan, these classes are taught by some of the most influential historians, authors, and academics in the country.&#160;</p><p>Most of the courses below are either completely free or free to audit (meaning you won't receive a grade or certification of completion). If you do want a certificate to add to your resume or LinkedIn, prices vary from $25-$196, depending on the class and learning platform.&#160;</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">10 courses that will teach you more about American politics and government:</strong></h2>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tHardvardX's US Government XSeries Program\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96ef98f21803001222befb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"girl online learning\" height=\"3264\" width=\"4352\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">INDRANIL MUKHERJEE / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&#38;xs=1&#38;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fxseries%2Fharvardx-us-government\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on edX, $196 for a certificate</a></h3><p>If your memory of learning about the three branches of government in middle school is foggy at best, this four-part HarvardX series will do more than just catch you up to speed. In this self-paced program, you'll start with the foundations of the US Constitution before tackling the inner workings of the Federal government and public policy. While this set of classes costs $196, you'll receive about four months'-worth of educational content and a certificate at the end (this can be a great option if you're looking to study or work in politics in the future).</p>\n\tAfrican American History: From Emancipation to the Present\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f03a4743a3001216b9ef?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman on laptop outside\" height=\"2640\" width=\"3519\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ute Grabowsky / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://oyc.yale.edu/african-american-studies/afam-162\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Available on Open Yale Courses, free</a>&#160;</h3><p>Like the title suggests, this class covers Black history from when slavery was abolished, spanning all the way through the Bill Clinton era of politics. It includes 25 completely free video lectures, most of them two-part classes on specific topics including Migration and Urbanization and the Black Power movement. There's also a long syllabus with texts from Martin Luther King, Jr., James Baldwin, Malcolm X, Angela Davis, and Anita Hill, among many others.&#160;</p>\n\tDoris Kearns Goodwin Teaches US Presidential History and Leadership\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96effbf21803001222befd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman on laptop outside\" height=\"2652\" width=\"3536\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Cindy Ord / Staff / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&#38;u=1088116&#38;m=62509&#38;urllink=www.masterclass.com%2Fclasses%2Fdoris-kearns-goodwin-teaches-us-presidential-history-and-leadership\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on MasterClass, $15 per month or $180 annual membership</a></h3><p>Pulitzer-winning historian Doris Kearns Goodwin spent over 50 years studying US presidents and shares everything she learned about the greatest ones. From Lincoln to FDR, she examines the core qualities of influential leadership, focusing this course on the emotional aspects of being a memorable president. As a bonus, this class doubles as personal development training, as many of the points can apply to your own career, ending with notes on how to apply what you learned to your own activism.&#160;</p>\n\tFighting for Equality: 1950-2018\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f0ad4743a3001216b9f2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"man on laptop outside\" height=\"2312\" width=\"3083\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">SOPA Images / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&#38;xs=1&#38;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fcourse%2Ffighting-for-equality-19502018\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on edX, free to audit, $50 for a certificate</a>&#160;</h3><p>If you missed your chance to take Women's Studies in high school or college, this Columbia University course provides a thorough look at women's fight for equal rights in America. Starting from the Cold War era, the class explores the growth of the 1960s feminist movement all the way through the 2016 election, #MeToo movement, and 2018 midterms. Beyond covering history, the class also asks you to consider some tough conundrums, such as the times when equality for some women may result in inequality for others, or how to best move forward without leaving other women behind.</p>\n\tAmerican Capitalism: A History\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f269f21803001222bf14?format=jpeg\" alt=\"girl online learning\" height=\"3383\" width=\"4511\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">KONTROLAB / Getty images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&#38;xs=1&#38;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fcourse%2Famerican-capitalism-a-history\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on edX, free to audit, $25 for a certificate</a></h3><p>Capitalism continues to be a major subject of contention, but it's far from as simple as it seems on the surface. Offered through Cornell, this four-week course explores American capitalism's 500+ year history, tracking its many changes even as its core tenets (such as wage labor and private property) remained the same. The class will also touch upon global capitalism as well, while also acknowledging the US's unique role in it.&#160;</p>\n\tDemocratic to Authoritarian Rule\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f30e4743a3001216ba0b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman online learning\" height=\"2750\" width=\"3666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Aziz Karimov / Getty images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&#38;xs=1&#38;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fcourse%2Fdemocratic-to-authoritarian-rule\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on edX, free to audit, $25 for a certificate&#160;</a></h3><p>As many international political systems have started to shift into authoritarianism, understanding how and why it happens is crucial to safeguarding democracy. Featuring guest contributors from Columbia, the University of Michigan, and Rutgers, this course brings expert perspectives to explore the processes that undermine and eventually erode democratic structures, leaving learners with a better knowledge of contemporary politics.&#160;</p>\n\tHow to Avoid Logical Fallacies\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f374f21803001222bf20?format=jpeg\" alt=\"professor online teaching\" height=\"2671\" width=\"3562\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Horacio Villalobos / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=EHFxW6yx8Uo&#38;mid=40328&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.coursera.org%2Flearn%2Flogical-fallacies\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on Coursera, free with 7-day trial, $49 per month after trial ends</a></h3><p>The ability to identify and unpack flimsy arguments is almost as important as understanding key political issues themselves. In the fourth installment of a larger series on logic and critical thinking, this course goes through all the types of logical fallacies you might hear in speeches and debates, while also equipping you with the tools you'll need to argue against lies and exaggerations when you spot them.</p>\n\tMoral Foundations of Politics\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f3fff21803001222bf26?format=jpeg\" alt=\"girl on laptop\" height=\"3106\" width=\"4142\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">MediaNews Group / Reading Eagle via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=EHFxW6yx8Uo&#38;mid=40328&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.coursera.org%2Flearn%2Fmoral-politics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on Coursera, free to audit, $49 for a certificate&#160;</a></h3><p>The core of most political debates &#8212; whether they're over economic inequality, healthcare reform, or the concept of free speech &#8212; is morality. To explore the moral foundations of politics, this Yale course dives into major political theories of the Enlightenment, such as utilitarianism and Marxism, examining them in both a historical and modern context. You'll leave the course with a firmer foundation for your own political arguments, with knowledge on how to apply these ideas to political discussions today.</p>\n\tAct on Climate: Steps to Individual, Community, and Political Action\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f4a14743a3001216ba18?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman online teaching\" height=\"3520\" width=\"4694\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ethan Miller / Staff / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=EHFxW6yx8Uo&#38;mid=40328&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.coursera.org%2Flearn%2Fact-on-climate\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on Coursera, free to audit, $49 for a certificate&#160;</a></h3><p>If you're concerned about climate change but feel powerless to do anything, this course outlines the manageable, individual actions you can take to make a difference, whether you're focusing on food, energy, or transportation. It also teaches you how to engage your local community in environmental causes, so you're left with tangible steps to making a significant difference.</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tHow the US Government Works and How to Get Involved\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f582f21803001222bf31?format=jpeg\" alt=\"girl online learning\" height=\"3024\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Francois LOCHON / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&#38;xs=1&#38;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.edx.org%2Fcourse%2Fhow-the-us-government-works-how-to-get-involved\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Available on edX, free to audit, $49 for a certificate</a></h3><p>Keeping up with the news brings one major downside: It can start to get really overwhelming, especially if you feel like your voice will never be heard. Luckily, this course is designed to combat those familiar feelings of apathy and hopelessness, by providing you with the tools you need to stay effectively engaged with your local and federal government. Led by Georgetown faculty, this self-paced course covers the functions of the three branches of government, the steps to joining an interest group, and the role news and media organizations play in politics.</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/online-us-politics-government-history-classes'>Business The ads will then drive shoppers to their Shopify stores for checkout.</p><p>The new TikTok channel means Shopify merchants can access core functions of the TikTok For Business Ads Manager without leaving the Shopify dashboard.
