Hitij/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Tesla paid Elon Musk $3 million to personally insure company directors against legal expenses, a new filing revealed on Wednesday.</li>\n<li>Musk provided up to $100 million \"from his personal funds\" for the indemnification agreement, which lasted 90 days.</li>\n<li>Tesla announced in April that Musk would personally insure its board members because of \"disproportionately high premiums\" among insurers.</li>\n<li>The unusual arrangement ended after 90 days, and Tesla now has a more conventional form of insurance.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Tesla paid its CEO Elon Musk $3 million after the billionaire personally offered up to $100 million in indemnity coverage to company directors, a <a href=\"https://ir.tesla.com/node/21221/html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://ir.tesla.com/node/21221/html\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">new filing</a> showed on Wednesday.</p><p>Tesla announced in April that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-personally-insures-tesla-board-members-citing-high-premiums-2020-4?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Musk would personally insure its board members</a> because of \"disproportionately high premiums\" quoted by insurance companies for the indemnity coverage. The coverage protects directors from having to pay for their own defense, settlements, or judgments against them, if they face expensive lawsuits.</p><p>In Wednesday's filing, the electric-vehicle company said it entered a 90-day \"indemnification agreement\" with its founder and CEO in June. Within this agreement, Musk provided up to $100 million \"from his personal funds\" for indemnity coverage, the filing said.</p><p>\"In return, we agreed to pay our CEO a total of $3 million which represents the market-based premium ... as prorated for 90 days and further discounted by 50%,\" the filing said.</p><p>Tesla had previous said it would pay Musk at least&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-pays-elon-musk-1-million-insure-board-3-months-2020-7\">$1 million</a> for the coverage.</p><p>The agreement ended after the 90-day period, and Tesla said it has \"instead bound a customary directors' and officers' liability insurance policy with third-party carriers.\" It didn't specify which carriers had been chosen.</p><p>At the same time that the indemnification agreement was made in June, investor adviser PIRC urged Tesla shareholders <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-pays-elon-musk-1-million-insure-board-3-months-2020-7\">to vote Musk out as CEO</a> over his $55.8 billion bonus pay package.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-elon-musk-insurance-payment-indemnity-lawsuits-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 27 Oct 2020 15:18:49 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f72324774fe5b0018a8dcf0?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"79996710f192552dcac3fba538275440","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn37@2020_6/2020/10/27/16-54-11-761_c50a8a1048f18b5d.webp","destWidth":2666,"destHeight":2000,"sourceBytes":104646,"destBytes":104646,"author":"insider@insider.com (Kate Duffy)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f71db5974fe5b0018a8db56?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn7@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-54-04-385_a7d8bb7c62bca4f1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626676},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"These key psychological differences can determine whether you're liberal or conservative","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/psychological-differences-between-conservatives-and-liberals-2018-2","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a8eda59391d941c008b4639?format=jpeg\" alt=\"womens march\" height=\"799\" width=\"1066\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A crowd at the Women&#39;s March on Washington, DC on January 21, 2017.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shannon Stapleton/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Liberals and conservatives don't just differ politically. According to research, members either side of the political spectrum differ psychologically.&#160;</li>\n<li>Here is a list of the 15 biggest psychological differences between liberals and conservatives.&#160;</li>\n<li>People who feel fear more often are more likely to lean conservative, whereas people who feel safer generally lean more liberal.&#160;</li>\n<li>Liberals and conservatives also tend to show compassion to different groups of people.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><br>Politically, Americans are <a href=\"http://www.people-press.org/2017/10/05/the-partisan-divide-on-political-values-grows-even-wider/\">highly divided.</a></p><p>When it comes to issues of race, immigration, national security,&#160;and environmental protection, they disagree about how the government should handle things like never before.</p><p>Relative to polls in the 1990s, Republicans are now much more likely to say poor people have it easy, while Democrats are less likely to say so. Conservatives are also more likely to say that environmental regulations are costing the US too many jobs. Liberals now seem less convinced that peace can be achieved through military strength than they were decades ago.&#160;</p><p>The Pew Research Center reports that the country's political divisions now <span>far exceed \"divisions along basic demographic lines, such as age, education, gender and race.\" The share of Americans who sit in the middle of the political spectrum is lower, too.</span></p><p><span><a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/twitter-found-more-russian-bots-trump-interacted-with-many-2018-1\">Russian bots have taken advantage</a> of these widening differences on Facebook and Twitter in an attempt to drive Americans' opinions further apart.&#160;</span></p><p>But what in the brains of conservative and liberal voters actually drive their belief systems?&#160;Scientists have been researching the psychological differences between people with different stances, and there are a few key ways that people on opposite ends of the political spectrum see the world. Here's what the data shows:</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tBeing scared can make you more conservative.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9846680c60aa00190d4861?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Scared person\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Klaus Vedfelt/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"http://faculty.virginia.edu/haidtlab/jost.glaser.political-conservatism-as-motivated-social-cog.pdf\">Decades of research</a> have shown that people get more conservative when they feel threatened and afraid.</p><p>Threats of terrorism make everyone less liberal &#8212; researchers found this was especially true in the months after 9/11. During that time, the US saw a <a href=\"https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s11211-009-0098-z\">conservative shift</a>,&#160;and Americans displayed increased support for military spending and for President George W. Bush.</p><p>Americans aren't the only ones whose political leanings are influenced by fear. A <a href=\"http://faculty.virginia.edu/haidtlab/jost.glaser.political-conservatism-as-motivated-social-cog.pdf\">2003 review of research</a> conducted in five countries looked at 22 separate tests of the hypothesis that fear fuels conservative viewpoints and found it was universally true.</p>\n\tA conservative brain is more active in different areas than a liberal one.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9847a60c60aa00190d486d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trump Supporter\" height=\"682\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jeff Swensen / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Brain&#160;<a href=\"https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3092984/\">scans</a>&#160;show that people who self-identify as conservative have larger and&#160;<a href=\"http://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0052970\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">more active</a>&#160;right amygdalas, an area of the brain that's associated with expressing and processing fear. This aligns with the idea that feeling afraid makes people lean more to the right.&#160;</p><p>One 2013&#160;<a href=\"http://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0052970\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">study showed</a>&#160;conservative brains tend to have more activity in their right amygdalas when they're taking risks than liberals do.</p>\n\tOn the other hand, feeling safe and endowed with strength might make you lean a little more liberal than you otherwise would.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8077b0ea74820019ca62de?format=jpeg\" alt=\"women biden supporters\" height=\"2729\" width=\"3639\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Supporters attend a campaign event with Dr. Jill Biden, wife of Democratic U.S. presidential nominee Joe Biden, at Utepils Brewery on October 3, 2020 in Minneapolis, Minnesota.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Stephen Maturen/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-turn-conservatives-liberal-john-bargh-psychology-2017-10\">Groundbreaking research</a>&#160;that Yale psychologists published&#160;in 2017 revealed that helping people imagine they're completely safe from harm can make them (temporarily) hold more liberal views on social issues.</p><p>The authors of that study said their results suggest that socially conservative views are driven, at least in part, by people's need to feel safe and secure.</p><p>That finding didn't hold true for people with economically conservative views, though.</p>\n\tLiberals are less squeamish about looking at yucky stuff like vomit, feces, and blood.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9849460c60aa00190d4880?format=jpeg\" alt=\"PPE\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">skaman306/Getty. Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>A <a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/liberals-and-conservatives-process-disgust-and-empathy-differently-2018-1\">2018 study</a> of college students showed that those with more socially conservative views were quicker to&#160;physically look away from disgusting images &#8212; like pictures of blood, feces, or vomit &#8212; than their liberal peers.</p><p>The self-reported social conservatives also stared longer at photos of other people reacting in disgust to icky stuff.</p><p>This research backs up <a href=\"http://yoelinbar.net/papers/pathogens_politics.pdf\">other studies</a> that have suggested conservatives are more easily grossed out than liberals.</p><p>A gut reaction of disgust is, evolutionarily speaking, a good thing for survival, since it helps humans keep some foreign and potentially dangerous secretions at bay. But in our modern world, <a href=\"https://www.scholars.northwestern.edu/en/publications/germs-and-the-out-group-chronic-and-situational-disease-concerns-\">some research</a> suggests this kind of aversion toward \"impure\" pathogens may also impact how people see other people who aren't like them, including social \"out-groups\" like immigrants or foreigners.</p>\n\tConservatives tend to display more ordered thinking patterns, whereas liberals have more \"aha\" moments.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f76479874fe5b0018a8e9ae?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Dark circles tired stressed\" height=\"1387\" width=\"1850\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Peter Dazeley/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>A <a href=\"http://www.tandfonline.com/doi/full/10.1080/17470218.2015.1136338?scroll=top&#38;needAccess=true\">2016 study at Northwestern University</a> found that when conservative and liberal college students were given word problems to solve, both groups managed to arrive at some correct answers through gradual, analytical analysis.</p><p>But when feeling stuck on a problem, liberals were much more likely to draw upon a sudden burst of insight &#8212; an 'aha' moment, like a lightbulb turning on in the brain.&#160;</p><p>This didn't mean that the liberals were any smarter than the conservatives. Rather, it showed that their brains had a tendency to reorganize their thoughts in more flexible ways, while the conservatives tended to take a more step-by-step approach. The researchers suggested this finding may indicate that liberals and conservatives prefer solving problems in different ways.&#160;</p><p>Lead study author Carola Salvi said the results were consistent with what scientists already knew about the brains of people with different political leanings.</p><p>\"Conservatives have more structured and persistent cognitive styles,\" <a href=\"https://news.northwestern.edu/stories/2016/03/political-insight-republicans-democrats-conservatives-liberals-think-differently\">she said in a statement</a>.</p>\n\tLiberals tend to follow the wandering gaze of others more often, while conservative eyes stay more focused on the original subject they're looking at.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9849070c60aa00190d487d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Focused person\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tom Werner/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In 2010, researchers at the <a href=\"https://link.springer.com/article/10.3758%2Fs13414-010-0001-x\">University of Nebraska</a>&#160;tested whether conservatives and liberals physically see the world in different ways. They found that when it comes to matching the gaze of other people, the two groups differ.</p><p>The scientists measured this by having individual study participants watch a certain point on a computer screen and wait for a ball to show up in the frame. Then they added a distracting human face on the screen before the ball appeared. The face's eyes would look around. The scientists watched their participants to see if they followed the wandering gaze.</p><p>The researchers found that the liberal participants tended to follow the direction of the eyes on the screen. Conservatives, on the other hand, weren't as swayed by their pixelated peers, and kept waiting for the ball.</p><p>That finding surprised the study authors.&#160;</p><p>\"We did not expect conservatives to be completely immune to these cues,\" lead <a href=\"https://www.sciencedaily.com/releases/2010/12/101209074403.htm\">author Michael Dodd said</a> when the study was released.&#160;</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tHolding conservative views seems to make people more resistant to change and help them explain inequality.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a7c93be6e4a051e008b456e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"berkeley homeless\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>People gather on the sidewalk along Telegraph Avenue in Berkeley, California December 9, 2014. Gray-haired activists still hand out leaflets on Telegraph Avenue in Berkeley, but the California university town that has seen violent protests over police killings of unarmed black men is a far cry from the leftist hotbed that was the face of the anti-Vietnam War movement of the 1960s. Picture taken December 9, 2014.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Robert Galbraith/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>A <a href=\"http://faculty.virginia.edu/haidtlab/jost.glaser.political-conservatism-as-motivated-social-cog.pdf\">2003 review</a> of decades of research on conservative people suggested that their social views can help satisfy \"psychological needs\" to make sense of the world and manage uncertainty and fear.</p><p>\"People embrace political conservatism (at least in part) because it serves to reduce fear, anxiety, and uncertainty; to avoid change, disruption, and ambiguity; and to explain, order, and justify inequality among groups and individuals,\" <a href=\"http://faculty.virginia.edu/haidtlab/jost.glaser.political-conservatism-as-motivated-social-cog.pdf\">the researchers said</a>.&#160;</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tLiberal and conservative tastes in music and art are different, too.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a031dc542fd753a5a423dcf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"art gallery\" height=\"1335\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\\\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mary Turner/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"http://faculty.virginia.edu/haidtlab/jost.glaser.political-conservatism-as-motivated-social-cog.pdf\">Studies from the 1980s</a> showed that conservatives preferred more simple paintings, familiar music, and unambiguous texts and poems, while liberals enjoyed more cubist and abstract art.</p><p>Although that research dates back to a drastically different political climate, the findings hold up in more recent studies from <a href=\"https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0191886997001311?via%3Dihub\">1997</a>, <a href=\"http://www.drtomascp.com/uploads/ConsenualMusic_PACA_2010.pdf\">2010</a> and&#160;<a href=\"http://pubs.sciepub.com/education/3/8/17/\">2015</a>. In 2014, Time magazine conducted <a href=\"http://time.com/8293/its-true-liberals-like-cats-more-than-conservatives-do/\">an online survey</a> and found that conservative readers tended to say they'd rather visit Times Square than the Metropolitan Museum of Art.&#160;</p><p>The finding fits with other research that indicates conservatives tend to avoid uncertainty and dislike ambiguity more than their liberal counterparts.</p>\n\tLiberals are more likely to describe themselves as compassionate and optimistic, while conservatives are more likely to say they're people of honor and religion.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9849dc861cb70019936adf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Biden supporters\" height=\"682\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Drew Angerer / Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>A <a href=\"http://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/00221325.1980.10532816?journalCode=vgnt20\">1980 study of US high school students</a> found that conservative students at that time were more likely to describe themselves as \"responsible,\" \"organized,\" \"successful,\" and \"ambitious,\" while liberal students might describe themselves as \"loving,\" \"tender,\" or \"mellow.\"</p><p>Surveys suggest that today's adults aren't much different than those 80s kids. A <a href=\"http://www.people-press.org/2014/06/26/section-9-patriotism-personal-traits-lifestyles-and-demographics/\">Pew Research Center study</a> from 2014 showed that liberals were more likely than social conservatives to describe themselves as compassionate, trusting, upbeat, and optimistic, while conservatives were more likely to say they were people of honor, duty, religion, and proud to be American.&#160;</p><p>The self-reports go along with&#160;<a href=\"http://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0050092\">research from 2012</a>&#160;that suggested liberals' top moral concerns tend to be about compassion and fairness, while conservatives are more concerned with loyalty, tradition, respect for authority, and purity.</p>\n\tConservatives believe they have more self-control.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e84b56d487c224e270d1526?format=jpeg\" alt=\"concerned worried stressed\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.co.uk/detail/photo/concerned-woman-in-coffee-shop-royalty-free-image/1137382630\" target=\"_blank\">Rafael Elias / Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>One <a href=\"http://www.pnas.org/content/112/27/8250\">2015 study</a> found that conservative students were often better at focusing their attention on a cognitive task called the Stroop color and word test. The&#160;common psychological study tool asks&#160;participants to quickly name the correct color of a word that's written on a different color background.</p><p>In the study, conservative students seemed to&#160;correctly answer the color questions faster than their liberal peers. The researchers think that's because the conservatives were more likely to believe in the concept of self-control.</p><p>\"What we're finding is that conservatives are more likely to believe they can control their own behavior,\" psychologist Joshua Clarkson from the University of Cincinnati&#160;<a href=\"http://www.uc.edu/news/NR.aspx?id=21891\">said when his study was released</a>.</p><p>But the conservatives didn't always out-perform the liberals. When they were told that their free will might undermine their own self-control, they performed worse than their liberal peers.</p><p>\"One could imagine a host of situations where knowing you are responsible for your actions could lead to frustration, anxiety and other negative emotions that could impair self-control,\" Clarkson said.</p>\n\tLiberals and conservatives extend feelings of compassion to different people.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5a8f44900c157c24008b459e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"US President Donald Trump hugging flag\" height=\"768\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joe Raedle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/liberals-and-conservatives-process-disgust-and-empathy-differently-2018-1\">New research</a> finds&#160;that conservatives tend to express compassion to smaller social circles than liberals.</p><p>For example, conservative voters were&#160;found to be more likely to agree with statements like: \"I often have tender, concerned feelings for my family members who are less fortunate than me.\"</p><p>But their responses suggested such feelings did not extend to people from other countries.</p><p>Liberals, on the other hand, were more likely to feel that same level of compassion for people around the world, and even to non-human and imaginary subjects like animals and aliens.</p><p>\"Conservatives self-report more parochialism in that they tend to expend their empathy toward more well-defined, closed social circles like the family whereas liberals self-report more universalism in that they expend their empathy toward more permeable, broader social circles like the world as a whole,\" Dr. Adam Waytz, professor at Northwestern's Kellogg School of Management, told Insider.&#160;</p>\n\tConservatives report a greater meaning of life and more satisfaction than liberals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2e7b905af6cc1e29604c63?format=jpeg\" alt=\"black trump supporter\" height=\"1000\" width=\"1333\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Supporters of President Donald Trump rally to reopen California on May 16, 2020 in Woodland Hills, California.\n<p class=\"copyright\">David McNew/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/1948550618768241\">Researchers at the University of Southern California</a> conducted a study in 2018 on the theory that conservatives tend to be more satisfied in life than liberals.&#160;</p><p>Their findings suggested the theory is actually true.&#160;</p><p>The data compiled from five portions of the study on different groups of people found conservatives overall reported greater meaning and purpose in life.&#160;</p><p>The study also found satisfaction in life related more closely to social conservativism rather than those who identified just as economically conservative.&#160;</p>\n\tTrump supporters suggests they have more in common with Trump's personal and professional values than his political leanings.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/58111109b28a642b0f8b4812?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump supporters\" height=\"3361\" width=\"4884\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Supporters rally with Republican U.S. presidential nominee Donald Trump in Tampa, Florida, on October 24, 2016.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomson Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>A <a href=\"https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0191886918300862\">survey of 1.825 people</a>&#160;conducted on the internet in March 2016 revealed that Trump supporters were more likely to connect with his overall personality and outlook on money than they were to support his politics.</p><p>The survey respondents tended to agree with statements like \"people who are poor just need to work harder\" and \"vacations are for weaklings,\" while disagreeing with statements like \"I try to stay out of the spotlight\" and \"I don't like to gamble.\"&#160;</p><p>The study authors said these kinds of personal values were better predictors of support for then-candidate Trump than party affiliations or political ideologies.&#160;</p><p>\"Trump supporters... ...seek power over others, are motivated by wealth accumulation, and prefer conformity, hierarchy, and clear-cut rules for behavior,\" the authors wrote in their paper, published <a href=\"https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0191886918300862\">online in the journal Personality and Individual Differences</a> in February 2018.</p><p>The researchers think these perceptions of shared values between candidates and constituents probably play into everyone's voting behavior, not just that of Trump supporters.</p>\n\tA study found that voters who were aggressive, angry kids were more likely to distrust the government and lean liberal as adults.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ad52085146e7128008b4b23?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Yelling kid\" height=\"2095\" width=\"2793\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Stobe/Getty Images for New York Red Bulls</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>A <a href=\"http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/full/10.1177/0956797617742159\">longitudinal study</a> of more than 16,000 people in the UK found that those who were more aggressive as youngsters (when they were 5-7 years old) became more economically liberal and mistrusting of the government as adults in their early 30s.&#160;</p><p>\"Children who showed higher levels of conduct problems &#8212; that is, aggression, fighting, stealing from peers &#8212; were more likely to be economically left-leaning and distrustful of the political system as adults,\" study author and psychologist Gary Lewis from the University of London <a href=\"https://www.psychologicalscience.org/news/releases/adults-political-leanings-linked-with-early-personality-traits.html\">said in a release</a>.</p><p>\"Some, but not all, of this link was explained by educational attainment and socioeconomic status in adulthood.\"&#160;</p>\n\tBoth think they're always being fair.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f91e2a4abcd0c0018d692ca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"joe biden rally\" height=\"682\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>A <a href=\"https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/full/10.1177/0146167218798822\">2018 study by researchers at Stanford University</a> found liberals and conservatives both think they judge people of all political backgrounds equally for their actions based on their moral codes.&#160;</p><p>However, the findings suggested while liberals and conversations both think they are applying their judgment equally they actually both tend to judge members of their own ideology more favorably than those outside, even if they committed the same action.&#160;</p><p>\"It seems that most people think that they applying their moral principles in an even-handed way. However, our findings suggest that we humans struggle to apply our moral principles equally to our outgroups and ingroups,\" <a href=\"https://www.psypost.org/2019/08/ingroup-versus-outgroup-thinking-warps-the-moral-principles-of-liberals-and-conservatives-54277\">authors Dr. Jan Voelkel and Dr. Mark Brandt told PsyPost.</a></p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/psychological-differences-between-conservatives-and-liberals-2018-2'>Business af6cc1e29604c63?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn48@2020_6/2020/10/27/16-54-03-941_afbd908de7f9df03.webp","https://i.insider.com/58111109b28a642b0f8b4812?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn9@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-54-06-330_cd98a7b3e338268b.webp","https://i.insider.com/5ad52085146e7128008b4b23?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn84@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-08-619_c542e0fd7cc95d29.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f91e2a4abcd0c0018d692ca?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn37@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-10-326_71687dba78c650c1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626752},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 href=\"https://khn.org/news/covid-spikes-exacerbate-health-worker-shortages-in-rocky-mountains-great-plains__trashed/?utm_campaign=KHN%3A%20First%20Edition&utm_medium=email&_hsmi=98236680&_hsenc=p2ANqtz-_yBecJR0k2wC_z09Hm45AENKj8MDaOwbjJoPxZtZgxVnK4wL_YG1sJ6KEsn2oLcOSHmKe5V2awPJM_IF4TxsphqFnd7A&utm_content=98236680&utm_source=hs_email;utm_source=hs_email\">beginning to face a shortage of health workers</a> able to respond to patients in need of care.</p><p>In an attempt to get in front of these looming concerns, Utah hospitals will begin to ration care in the Doctors in the state compiled a list of criteria that will determine which patients are able to stay in overcrowded intensive-care units and which will be booted to prioritize the most dire cases.</p><p>Hospital administrators presented the criteria to Gov. Gary Herbert to be \"activated if this trend continues,\" Greg Bell, president of the Utah Hospital Association, told the Tribune, adding, \"and we see no reason why it won't.\"</p><p>Over the weekend, a county judge in El Paso, Texas, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/virus-outbreak-el-paso-texas-greg-abbott-e9b8a22bd64e718834887ead7d236ddd\">issued a stay-at-home order</a> in response to a rising number of overwhelmed hospitals.</p><p>Idaho is also bolstering its safety precautions due to coronavirus spikes and overcrowded hospitals. Gov. Brad Little on Monday announced the state will again tighten indoor and outdoor capacity limits to curtail the spread of the coronavirus.</p><figure></figure><p>\"Hospitals throughout the state are quickly filling up or are already full with COVID-19 patients and other patients, and way too many health care workers are out sick with COVID-19,\" Little said, according to <a href=\"https://www.idahostatesman.com/news/coronavirus/article246720586.html\">the Idaho Statesman</a>.</p><p>Each of these states has seen surges in the number of confirmed COVID-19 cases in recent weeks.</p><p>Meanwhile, President Donald Trump continues to hammer home the message that the coronavirus is overhyped. Speaking at multiple rallies and posting a string of tweets between Saturday and Tuesday, Trump once again downplayed the virus and claimed it's \"<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-says-us-rounding-turn-covid-19-even-cases-surge-2020-10\">rounding the turn</a>,\" a phrase that's inconsistent with data showing surges in infection rates.</p><p>\"The Fake News Media is riding COVID, COVID, COVID, all the way to the Election! WE ARE ROUNDING THE TURN!!!\" he <a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1321051933654863872\">tweeted</a> Tuesday.</p><p>Trump's claims go against the predictions made by <a href=\"https://www.wndu.com/2020/10/26/michigan-health-officials-round-table-to-discuss-coronavirus-surge/\">local</a> <a href=\"https://wsvn.com/news/local/miami-dade/south-florida-works-to-prevent-second-surge-of-covid-19-cases-ahead-of-holiday-season/\">health officials</a> across the country. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pandemic-fatigue-looms-record-high-new-daily-covid-19-cases-2020-10\">Data also indicate</a> positive cases are rising in multiple states.</p><p>Hospitals are trying to respond to the surging cases by allocating and rationing people, power, and medical materials. But the medical facilities and resources remain at risk of inundation and overcrowding if cases continue to spike.</p><p>At the height of the pandemic in March, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-hospitals-face-shortages-of-equipment-staff-and-beds-2020-3\">experts warned</a> that shortages across the healthcare system might make caring for sick patients significantly harder.</p><p>The coronavirus has so far infected more than 8.7 million people in the United States, according to the latest data compiled by Johns Hopkins University. Of that, more than 225,000 people have died.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/spiking-coronavirus-cases-overwhelming-hospitals-experts-warn-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 27 Oct 2020 15:19:28 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f981a6ff21803001222c26c?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"8c83d59b13b277c74535f5de7563e655","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn4@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-11-289_3f3c81bd454bc902.webp","destWidth":2538,"destHeight":1903,"sourceBytes":145432,"destBytes":145432,"author":"ydzhanova@businessinsider.com (Yelena Dzhanova)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f9830974743a3001216bdf4?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn68@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-54-02-073_4ba7832c7796c7af.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626693},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"If you struggle with staying awake at night, use this 4-step relaxation hack to fall asleep within minutes","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/military-pilots-sleep-trick-2-minutes-2019-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e53e466fee23d70d875e122?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FILE PHOTO: U.S. Army soldiers sleep in their chairs after returning to base during a 24 hour Cavalry &#34;Spur Ride&#34; for members of the US Army&#39;s 6th Squadron, 6th Cavalry Regiment in Fort Drum, New York September 30, 2010. The &#34;Spur Ride&#34; is a voluntary rite of passage where members of the U.S. Army Cavalry perform several physical tests utilizing their Army training and physical fitness while learning the history of the unit. This &#34;Spur Ride&#34; is the first for the unit in three years and comes shortly before deployment to Afghanistan.  REUTERS/Lucas Jackson\" height=\"2333\" width=\"3111\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>If you want to fall asleep faster, relax your body to reduce stress.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>During WWII, the US military realized that if fighter pilots didn't get sufficient sleep, they would make poor decisions on the job, which could have fatal consequences.</li>\n<li>The military brought expert Bud Winter to develop and test a scientifically designed relaxation technique, and Winter used it to teach the pilots how to fall asleep faster.</li>\n<li>After just six weeks of practice at turning their brains off using this five-step method, 96% of the pilots could fall asleep within 120 seconds.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories.</a></li>\n</ul><p dir=\"ltr\">For most of us, getting enough&#160;<a href=\"https://www.inc.com/melanie-curtin/the-sleep-hack-neuroscience-says-gives-your-brain-optimal-rest.html\">sleep</a>&#160;isn't a life-or-death kind of thing. Sure, we might make poor&#160;<a href=\"https://www.inc.com/rhett-power/5-keys-to-great-decision-making.html\">decisions</a>, but our being sleepy at the marketing meeting tomorrow is not going to get someone killed.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">During WWII, though, the US military quickly got hip to the fact that if fighter pilots didn't get sleep, their poor decisions had dire consequences. Their mishaps included errors that resulted in their being shot down — or shooting down guys on their own side.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Helping combat pilots get good rest fast became a priority.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">So the military brought in naval ensign Bud Winter to&#160;develop&#160;and test a scientifically designed&#160;method of \"teaching\" sleep. Winter was previously a successful college football coach&#160;who had collaborated&#160;with a psychology&#160;professor to form techniques to help athletes relax and excel under pressure.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">The relaxation hack Winter designed worked:&#160;After just six weeks of practice,&#160;<strong>96% of pilots could fall asleep within 120 seconds</strong>.&#160;Even with distractions like gunfire in the background. Even after drinking coffee. Even sitting up.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">If it works for combat pilots, it will work for you, regardless of how stressed you are about that meeting tomorrow. Here's how to do it.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">1. Get comfy</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Obviously, if you're in your bed, this is a non-issue. But if you're out and about, get into the most comfortable position that's feasible (i.e., lean your seat back if you're in your car; find the most comfortable chair in the conference room if you're napping at work).</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">2. Relax your face</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">This is key to the whole thing. You have 43 muscles in your face, and they're a big part of how your body knows whether you're stressed. When you fully relax your face, you send a physiological signal to your body that all is well. It's safe to sleep.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">So close your eyes and relax your whole face: forehead, cheeks, tongue, and jaw. You'll notice as you do this that your breathing naturally starts to deepen and slow.<iframe width=\"1\" height=\"1\" frameborder=\"0\" data-google-container-id=\"2\" data-load-complete=\"true\"></iframe></p><p dir=\"ltr\">Now make sure your eyes are fully relaxed. You have six muscles in your eye sockets; feel them all go limp.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">3. Release tension, starting with your shoulders</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Let them get heavy, and then let them go completely, as if they were falling down toward your feet. Let the back of your neck relax. Take a deep breath and let it out slowly, releasing any remaining tension (most people store most tension in their shoulders, necks, and jaws).</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Now your arms: Feel them get heavy and relax, starting with your dominant side. If you're right-handed, start with your right bicep and feel it relax. If it's not, tense it fully and then let it go slack. Repeat the process with your hands.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Let your legs go limp. Feel your right quad sinking down, getting heavier and heavier. Next your right calf, ankle, and foot. Repeat on the other side.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">4. Clear your mind for 10 seconds</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Now that you've fully relaxed your body, time to power down your thoughts. (This is like that moment after you switch your iPhone off when it takes another few seconds for it to fully turn off.)</p><p dir=\"ltr\">What you really want to avoid are any thoughts that involve movement (\"I've got to pick up that dry cleaning tomorrow\"; \"Did I remember to put out the recycling?\"). These actually prompt involuntary movement. You don't realize it, but just thinking about something causes micro-contractions in certain muscles.</p><p><a href=\"https://smile.amazon.com/gp/product/0498025411/ref=smi_www_rco2_go_smi_3905707922?_encoding=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0498025411&ie=UTF8&imprToken=HRDlUsa.69hW4-aUFpYR7Q&linkCode=w61&linkId=FSXA3GZUT5SFDAZ4&slotNum=0&tag=stucosuccess4&#38;slotNum=0&#38;tag=stucosuccess\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Bud Winter</a>, author of \"Relax and Win: Championship Performance,\" has some tips for what to \"think\" of instead — and remember, you're holding this for 10 seconds straight:<br><br><em>First, we want you to fantasize that it is a warm spring day and you are lying in the bottom of a canoe on a very serene lake. You are looking up at a blue sky with lazy, floating clouds. Do not allow any other thought to creep in. Just concentrate on this picture and keep foreign thoughts out, particularly thoughts with any movement or motion involved. Hold this picture and enjoy it for 10 seconds.</em><br><br><em>In the second sleep-producing fantasy, imagine that you are in a big, black, velvet hammock and everywhere you look is black. You must also hold this picture for 10 seconds.</em><br><br><em>The third trick is to say the words \"don't think ... don't think ... don't think,\" etc. Hold this, blanking out other thoughts for at least 10 seconds.</em></p><p dir=\"ltr\"><em>And that's it.&#160;When you have a fully relaxed body and a mind that's still for 10-plus seconds, you will fall asleep, period.</em></p><p dir=\"ltr\">Within two minutes, you'll be out like a light. Remember 96% of combat pilots achieved success after six weeks of practice. These weeks of practice are a worthwhile investment, because once you have it down, you can nap and sleep anywhere, which will dramatically improve your quality of life.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Sweet dreams.</p><p dir=\"ltr\"><em>This Inc. story was originally published on Business Insider on May 2, 2019.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5e53e466fee23d70d875e122?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"f70377edc40ea9afc4fedfe9b34736db","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn12@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-53-58-162_e08b6cbf913338d6.webp","destWidth":3111,"destHeight":2333,"sourceBytes":374542,"destBytes":374542,"author":"insider@insider.com (Melanie Curtin)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5e53e466fee23d70d875e122?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn12@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-53-58-162_e08b6cbf913338d6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626674},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"Vote in person if you're young and healthy — it's relatively safe, and your vote is more likely to count","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/voting-in-person-low-risk-more-reliable-than-mail-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f85b8dcc255d800190b98fa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Georgia voting\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Heather King waits in line at State Farm Arena, Georgia&#39;s largest early-voting location, to cast her ballot on October 12, 2020 in Atlanta.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jessica McGowan/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>More than 66 million Americans have already voted in this year's general election.&#160;</li>\n<li>Mail-in ballots are more likely to be rejected than ballots cast in person.&#160;</li>\n<li>The chances of contracting the coronavirus from voting in person are low, so if you're young and healthy, consider voting in person.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>More than <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/10/25/politics/pre-election-voting-surpasses-2016-early-ballots/index.html\">66 million Americans have already voted</a>. About <a href=\"https://electproject.github.io/Early-Vote-2020G/index.html\">44 million of those have voted by mail</a> – already far more than the 33 million mail-in votes cast in the 2016 election.</p><p>That's largely because of the coronavirus pandemic: Because of public-health concerns, most states allow voting by mail this year. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-vote-in-person-safely-november-election-2020-10\">All but five states are letting all (or nearly all) voters to mail their ballots</a>, and nearly 40% of American voters have said they plan to do so this year.&#160;</p><p>But if you are young and healthy, here's a suggestion: Don't vote by mail. Cast a ballot in person instead.&#160;</p><p>Experts do not consider going to a polling place any more dangerous than <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2020/09/voting-during-pandemic-pretty-safe/616084/\">a trip to the grocery store</a>, as long as voters follow common-sense safety protocols like mask-wearing and social distancing. And voting in person means your vote is more likely to be counted: Historically, only about .01% of in-person ballots <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2020/08/22/904693468/more-than-550-000-primary-absentee-ballots-rejected-in-2020-far-outpacing-2016\">get rejected</a>, compared with around 1% of mail-in ballots, though rejection rates vary significantly by state.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f85cc74c255d800190b998d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Virginia voting\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A woman casts her ballot for the 2020 election at an early voting location in Alexandria, Virginia, on October 1, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sarah Silbiger/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>This year, a greater percentage of ballots is likely to be rejected because more people are voting by mail in states that typically have higher rejection rates for mail-in ballots, like Georgia. According to a USA Today investigation, if 70 million voters cast ballots by mail in 2020,&#160;about 1 million ballots <a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/in-depth/news/investigations/2020/10/08/rejected-mail-ballots-projected-major-factor-2020-election/3576714001/\">could be rejected</a> overall. That may be enough to affect the outcome of the presidential election or other races.</p><p>What's more, ballot rejection rates could easily be higher this year than in the past, since a record number of people will vote by mail for the first time and may be more likely to make mistakes on their ballots.</p><p>Earlier this month, Michael Herron, a professor of government at Dartmouth University, found that first-time mail-in voters in Florida were <a href=\"http://www.dartmouth.edu/~herron/VBM_experience.pdf\">2.75 times more likely</a> to have their ballots rejected than people with vote-by-mail experience. That was primarily because the voters sent their ballots in late or didn't include signatures on envelopes.&#160;</p><p>Plus, states that haven't offered mail-in voting on such a wide scale before could have trouble tallying ballots speedily and accurately.</p><p>\"We've never had an election where mail voting is such a big deal,\"&#160;Herron&#160;told Business Insider. The importance of mail-in voting, he added, \"has focused attention on the issues\" with the current system – especially its high rejection rates.</p><p>Primary elections earlier this year offered a glimpse into how many mail-in ballots might get rejected come Election Day. More than <a href=\"https://theconversation.com/over-1-million-mail-in-ballots-could-be-rejected-in-the-us-election-and-the-rules-are-changing-by-the-day-148188\">550,000 mail-in primary ballots were rejected</a> out of a total of 26.6 million <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/10/13/mail-in-voting-became-much-more-common-in-2020-primaries-as-covid-19-spread/\">mail-in or absentee ballots</a>; that's nearly twice as many as in the 2016 November election, which had nearly 319,000 rejected ballots out of <a href=\"https://www.brookings.edu/policy2020/votervital/how-does-vote-by-mail-work-and-does-it-increase-election-fraud/\">33 million mail-in or absentee votes</a>.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4e93fb7ed0ee001e25cc62?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mail ballot\" height=\"1331\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A woman holds up a mail-in ballot before dropping it off at Boston City Hall during the Massachusetts state primary election on September 1, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">JOSEPH PREZIOSO/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>If, say, 2020's rejection rate for mail-in ballots turns out to be around 2%, that could mean as many as 2.15 million uncounted ballots this November. For reference, Hillary Clinton won the popular vote in 2016 by about 2.9 million votes.</p><h2><strong>Voting in person is a low-risk activity</strong></h2><p>During the 2020 primary elections, in-person voting didn't appear to sicken many people, a <a href=\"https://fivethirtyeight.com/features/voting-in-primaries-didnt-worsen-the-covid-19-pandemic/\">FiveThirtyEight analysis found</a>. Most experts now don't consider it to be especially risky.&#160;</p><p>\"I actually equate it with takeout,\" Saskia Popescu, an epidemiologist at the University of Arizona and leading expert on coronavirus transmission, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-vote-in-person-safely-november-election-2020-10\">previously told Business Insider</a>. \"There are so many safety protocols being put into place for safe voting that it is really a lower-risk activity.\"</p><p>That's because most polling places are taking extra precautions. For instance, <a href=\"https://www.dekalbcountyga.gov/voter-registration-elections/covid-19-safety-precautions\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"db9e054837f0360e845fc5451d043682\">in Dekalb County, Georgia</a>, poll workers will wear masks and face shields, and voting equipment will be cleaned at least once an hour. In <a href=\"https://recorder.maricopa.gov/pdf/Final%20November%202020%20General%20Election%20Day%20and%20Emergency%20Voting%20Plan%209-16-20.pdf\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"8b10d1a2ef3170ceab9db28b82a9ba26\">Maricopa County, Arizona</a>, all polling locations are expected to provide voters with gloves and masks, and to disinfect pens after each use.</p><p>\"Most polling stations are requiring masks, you're able to distance, and your time inside is very short,\" Popescu said.&#160;</p><h2><strong>Voting considerations don't affect everyone equally</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f8eeeb69e9fe4001900a4d1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pennsylvania voting \" height=\"1334\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Long lines of voters wait to cast early ballots at the A. B. Day School polling location on October 17, 2020 in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mark Makela/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Younger voters and voters of color – both Democratic-leaning groups – are <a href=\"http://www.dartmouth.edu/~herron/VBM_experience.pdf\">more likely to have their votes rejected.</a> Both groups have ballots disproportionately rejected for arriving late or not having signatures.</p><p>\"A lot of problems with signatures are associated with younger voters,\" Herron said.</p><p>For some young, healthy voters, then, these statistics present a clear choice. Their risk of getting seriously ill with COVID-19 is relatively low compared to people in other age brackets, and their risk of getting a ballot rejected is relatively high. So it makes sense to head to the polls.</p><p>But for many voters of color, the decision isn't straightforward. Black, Native, and Hispanic Americans have been hospitalized with and <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/covid-data/investigations-discovery/hospitalization-death-by-race-ethnicity.html\">died of COVID-19 at higher rates</a> than white Americans. But even Black voters who have plenty of experience mailing in their ballots are more likely to have them rejected than white voters, according to the analysis <a href=\"http://www.dartmouth.edu/~herron/VBM_experience.pdf\">by Herron's team.</a></p><p>It's a tough choice: Vote by mail, knowing that ballot has a higher chance of getting rejected, or go to the polls but face a higher risk of a severe case if one is exposed to the coronavirus.</p><p>\"I think we would all agree that voters shouldn't be in that situation,\" Herron said.</p><h2><strong>How to reduce your coronavirus risk when voting</strong></h2><p>The deadline for requesting a mail-in ballot has <a href=\"https://time.com/5889969/how-to-vote-by-mail/\">already passed</a> in some states. So if you still want to vote by mail but haven't requested a ballot yet (and you're not a resident of a universal vote-by-mail state), check as soon as possible to see whether you still can.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7f1a5d282c500018c794e3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"texas voting\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Election workers accept mail-in ballots from voters at a drive-through ballot drop-off site at NRG Stadium in Houston, Texas, on October 7, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Go Nakamura/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>If you vote in person, it's still worth taking extra precautions. Bring your own hand sanitizer and pen, wear a mask, stay 6 feet from other voters, and try to go to your polling place when it's not too crowded.&#160;</p><p>If your county offers the option to vote in your car, consider that. Places like <a href=\"https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/drive-voting-wait-time-technology-safety-measures-polls/story?id=73694980\">Harris County, Texas,</a> and <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/10/02/us/voting-in-california.html\">Orange County, California,</a> are hosting drive-through polling places that let voters roll down a window and pass a poll worker their ballots. The poll worker will check your signature, then you're good to go.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/voting-in-person-low-risk-more-reliable-than-mail-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 27 Oct 2020 16:32:00 stores","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/where-to-buy-stamps","description":"<p class=\"financial-disclaimer\"><i>When you buy through our links, we may earn money from our affiliate partners. <a href=\"https://www.insider-inc.com/commerce-on-insider-inc/\">Learn more.</a></i></p>\n<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96f624f21803001222bf37?format=jpeg\" alt=\"usps postage stamps\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption> \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Les Shu/Business Insider</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\">\n <li>Postage stamps are handy to have around for when you need to send greeting cards, invoices, or any other physical mail.</li>\n <li>To buy some, your local post office is a good place to start, but you don't need to step foot in one — you can order them from the US Postal Service's website.</li>\n <li>Grocery stores, pharmacies, and similar retailers often carry booklets of stamps, too.</li>\n <li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/insider-picks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/insider-picks\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Sign up for Insider Reviews' weekly newsletter for more buying advice and great deals.</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p>Whether you want to send a greeting card, mail in an absentee ballot, pay a bill, or connect with some <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/coronavirus-snail-mail-letters-better-than-zoom-2020-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">quarantine pen pals</a>, it's always useful to have some stamps on hand. It costs 55 cents to send a domestic one-ounce, standard-sized envelope through the <a href=\"https://www.usps.com/business/prices.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">United States Postal Service</a>, making it an affordable way to correspond with people in a tactile, memorable way.</p>\n<p>A booklet of 20 stamps comes out to around $11. The beauty of \"forever\" stamps is that you can still use them even when the price of mailing a letter goes up. That means if you find a roll of them from 2016, when the price was 47 cents, you can still stick it on an envelope today and drop it into a mailbox.</p>\n<p>There are lots of places you can pick up stamps, not just at the local post office. If you're in need of postage, here are the ways you can buy stamps.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>\n<h2>Your local post office</h2>\n<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f962856f21803001222bd7c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Post office self-service kiosk in New York City\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption>\n   A self-service kiosk at a post office in New York City. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Les Shu/Business Insider</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<p>This is a given, but depending on the time of the day, the customer service queue can get long. If you just need stamps, use one of the electronic self-service kiosks (where available) instead; there are usually no lines to use them. The downside is that you won't be able to buy specialty stamps.</p>\n<h2>USPS.com</h2>\n<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f96de574743a3001216b956?format=jpeg\" alt=\"usps online postal store stamps\" height=\"811\" width=\"1082\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption> \n   <p class=\"copyright\">USPS</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<p>The <a href=\"https://store.usps.com/store/results/stamps/_/N-9y93lv?_requestid=42317\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">post office's website</a> offers a variety of stamps, from the standard US Flag to seasonal (e.g., Christmas, Diwali, Halloween) and themed options (e.g., Bugs Bunny, American outdoors, moon landing), as well as notable Americans like Gwen Ifill, Sally Ride, Walt Whitman, and Arnold Palmer. The tyrannosaurus rex option is glossy and fun. The site lets you filter by color, shape, theme, denomination, and more.&nbsp;</p>\n<h2>Retailers</h2>\n<p>Everywhere from grocery stores to pharmacies to office supply stores often sell stamps. Instead of just chancing whether your local Publix or Kroger has them, you can find out using <a href=\"https://tools.usps.com/go/POLocatorAction.action\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">USPS's location tool</a>. Put in your zip code and choose \"national retailer\" from the drop-down location menu. Depending on where you live, you'll get results like Walgreens, Winn-Dixie, and Staples. Keep in mind that these locations often only sell booklets, so you won't be able to purchase stamps individually. And,&nbsp;most stores only carry them at their physical locations</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.costco.com/usps-first-class-forever-flag-stamp-100-count-.product.100404247.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Costco also sells stamps</a>, in 100-count batches, making it a good option for businesses and prolific letter writers. They aren't available online and may not be in every store location. <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=EHFxW6yx8Uo&amp;mid=38733&amp;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.samsclub.com%2Fp%2Fusps-forever-postage-stamps-lady-liberty-and-u-s-flag-100-stamps%2Fprod2320969%3Fxid%3Dpdp_carousel_rich-relevance.rr0_1ce.rr0_1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Sam's Club</a> will let you purchase stamps online, however.</p>\n<h3>USPS Forever First Class Postage Stamps (20-count)</h3>\n<div id=\"ProductCard_5f9829fbbf96b9246a2059b0\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\">\n <iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5f9829fbbf96b9246a2059b0&amp;type=button&amp;live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\" style=\"position:absolute; top:0; left: 0\"></iframe>\n</div>\n<h2>Banks</h2>\n<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9753744743a3001216bcc8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"us bank atm\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption>\n   Select US Bank ATMs offer stamps. To find a location, you can search via the bank's website. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">U.S. Bank</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<p>Some banks and credit unions sell stamps through their ATMs or tellers. This varies by the location, but the next time you are doing a transaction, check to see if they offer stamps as well. <a href=\"https://locations.usbank.com/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">US Bank</a> and <a href=\"https://www.53.com/content/fifth-third/en.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fifth Third Bank</a> let you filter by locations that sell stamps when you search for an ATM or branch on their websites. A representative for Wells Fargo said the bank is no longer selling stamps.</p>\n<h2>Other options</h2>\n<p>You can also request stamps from your mail carrier, who will provide you with an order form. You can order by phone at 1-800-STAMP-24 (800-782-6724). If your business needs to buy stamps in bulk, you can call that number or email <a href=\"mailto:StampsNow.info@usps.gov\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">StampsNow.info@usps.gov</a>. Those keen to start collecting can also page through the <a href=\"https://store.usps.com/store/product/stamp-collectors/usa-philatelic-P_012007\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">USA Philatelic catalog</a> and use its order form.</p>\n<p>Online services like <a href=\"https://www.stamps.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stamps.com</a> &nbsp;do allow you to print postage at home, but there's a monthly fee. If you just desperately need to mail something right now, you might be able to sign up for a free trial.&nbsp;</p>\n<p>Note: <a href=\"https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=999&amp;u=1088116&amp;m=17025&amp;urllink=www.minted.com%2Flp%2Fstationery-postage-stamp-pairs-stamp-pairs\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Minted</a>, <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&amp;xs=1&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.zazzle.com%2Fstore%2Fzazzle_stamps%2Fabout%2Fabout\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Zazzle</a>, and other gift sites used to sell personalized stamps, but the USPS discontinued the program in June 2020. to expand their majority in the House of Representatives after decisively flipping control of the chamber in the 2018 midterms.&#160;</li>\n<li>All 435 seats in the chamber are up for grabs. The House is currently composed of 232 Democrats, 197 Republicans, one Libertarian, and five vacancies.&#160;</li>\n<li>Election analysts say that Republicans have little to no chance of winning back the chamber altogether, with Democrats positioned to gain anywhere from five to 15 seats.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><bi-shortcode id=\"table-of-contents-sticky\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"h2\">Table of Contents: Masthead Sticky</bi-shortcode><p>All 435 seats in the House of Representatives are up for election this fall, with Democrats seeking to maintain and expand their control over the chamber along with battling to win back the White House and the US Senate.&#160;</p><p>In the 2018 midterms, Democrats flipped 40 seats in the House and won back the chamber altogether in a historic wave election – a repudiation of both President Donald Trump and the unified Republican government he presided over for nearly two years.</p><p>While Democrats have made inroads in exurban and rural places, the bulk of their gains in 2018 ran through America's suburbs, as college-educated whites and suburbanites fled the GOP in droves. That year, <a href=\"https://www.citylab.com/equity/2018/11/house-races-election-results-democrats-suburbs-blue-wave/575287/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"c25965fc02914d016b5aefacbb79e8c4\">according to data compiled by CityLab</a>, 22 of the 40 districts Democrats won back from Republican hands were located in dense suburban or sparse-suburban districts.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Currently, <a href=\"https://pressgallery.house.gov/member-data/party-breakdown\">the House is composed of</a> 232 Democrats, 197 Republicans, one Libertarian (Rep. Justin Amash of Michigan, who is retiring), and five vacancies that will be filled this November.&#160;</p><p>The most recent polling and fundraising trends indicate that Republicans are extremely unlikely to flip the 17 Democratic-controlled seats they'd need to win back the chamber altogether, and that Democrats are well-positioned to expand their majority by anywhere from five to fifteen seats, according to election analysts <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Redistrict/status/1315367252884062208\">at the Cook Political Report</a> and <a href=\"https://www.nationaljournal.com/s/710881?unlock=HOCWL6PWPJFSYUH9\">National Journal Hotline</a>.&#160;</p><p>But Republicans still have a shot at unseating some vulnerable Democrats, particularly Rep. Collin Peterson of Minnesota — who represents a district Trump carried by 30 points in 2016 — and a number of the Democrats who won back tough seats in 2018.</p><h2><strong>Insider's guides to the key US House seats up for election in 2020</strong></h2><h2><strong>Alaska</strong></h2><ul><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/alaska-at-large-house-election-don-young-alyse-galvin-2020\">AK-AL: Alyse Galvin takes on Republican Don Young in Alaska's At-Large Congressional District</a><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/alaska-at-large-house-election-don-young-alyse-galvin-2020\"><br></a></strong></li></ul><h2>Arizona</h2><ul><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/arizona-1st-district-house-election-tom-ohalleran-tiffany-shedd-2020\">AZ-01: Tiffany Shedd takes on Democrat Tom O'Halleran in Arizona's 1st Congressional District&#160;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/arizona-2nd-district-house-election-ann-kirkpatrick-brandon-martin-2020\">AZ-02: Democratic Rep. +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f9823abf21803001222c293?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"3077a81c0243ce005dcd9d9ab2799f24","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn81@2020_1/2020/10/27/16-54-09-618_9aed34fda9cb4485.webp","destWidth":2903,"destHeight":2177,"sourceBytes":406472,"destBytes":406472,"author":"kmclaughlin@businessinsider.com (Kelly McLaughlin)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f90ecfc212113001874010b?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn51@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-10-420_79d0947a09161798.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817626682},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:46","title":"How to save a webpage as a PDF on a Windows computer using the web browser of your choice","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-save-a-webpage-as-a-pdf-on-windows","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f973d544743a3001216bc84?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A businesswoman working on the computer\" height=\"1412\" width=\"1883\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Windows users can use any common web browser to save webpages as PDF articles.\n<p class=\"copyright\">nortonrsx/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>You can save a webpage as a PDF on a Windows computer using any installed web browser, including Microsoft Edge, Google Chrome, and Mozilla Firefox.</li>\n<li>To save any webpage as a PDF, you will need to access the browser's Print menu and select \"Save as PDF\" or \"Microsoft Print to PDF\" for your printing destination.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\">Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As the saying goes, nothing gets deleted from the internet — but sometimes it does change. You can avoid losing important information or even your work if you save it as a PDF.&#160;</p><p>Webpages are mutable, so they can change at any time the owner of the website sees fit. That's why it can be beneficial to save them as PDFs.</p><p>Saving webpages as PDFs allows you to access pages when you're offline, making it easier to reference them when you don't have an internet connection. Saving a webpage as a PDF also means that you have a permanent version, in case the owner of the site makes significant changes or deletes the site altogether.&#160;</p><p>On Windows computers, Microsoft Edge, Google Chrome, Firefox can save webpages as PDFs. Each interface looks only slightly different though the mechanism for printing is essentially the same.</p><p>Here's how to do it.&#160;</p><h2>How to save a webpage as a PDF on Windows in Google Chrome</h2><p><strong>1.</strong> Open the webpage you want to save.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.</strong> In the top right corner of the screen, click the three dots to bring down the browser menu.</p><p><strong>3.</strong> From the dropdown menu, choose \"Print.\"&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f973f4e4743a3001216bc94?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to save webpage as PDF on Windows 1\" height=\"768\" width=\"1366\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>This option won&#39;t automatically print the page but direct you to the Print menu.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abbey White/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4.</strong> The Print settings window will appear. Select the first dropdown menu, labeled \"Destination.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f973f7a4743a3001216bc96?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to save webpage as PDF on Windows 2\" height=\"768\" width=\"1366\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Click Destination to view print location options.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abbey White/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>5.</strong> Change the destination to \"Save as PDF.\"</p><p><strong>6.</strong> Click Save and wait for the \"Save As\" window to appear.</p><p><strong>7.</strong> Name the file, select the file destination, and then click \"Save.\"&#160;</p><h2>How to save a webpage as a PDF on Windows in Microsoft Edge</h2><p><strong>1.</strong> Open the webpage you want to save.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.</strong> In the top right corner of the screen, click the three dots to bring down the browser menu.</p><p><strong>3.</strong> From the dropdown menu, choose \"Print.\"&#160;</p><p><strong>4.</strong> The Print settings window will appear. Select the first dropdown menu beneath \"Print.\"</p><p><strong>5.</strong> Change the selection to \"Save as PDF.\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f97409f4743a3001216bc9d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to save webpage as PDF on Windows 3\" height=\"768\" width=\"1366\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>This will give you an option of saving and printer destinations.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abbey White/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>6.</strong> Click Save and wait for the \"Save As\" window to appear.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f974118f21803001222c1aa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to save webpage as PDF on Windows 4\" height=\"768\" width=\"1366\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You&#39;ll need to select which folder to save the PDF file to before you name it.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abbey White/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>7.</strong> Name the file, select the file destination, and then click \"Save.\"&#160;</p><h2>How to save a webpage as a PDF on Windows in Mozilla Firefox</h2><p><strong>1.</strong> Open the webpage you want to save.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.</strong> In the top right corner of the screen, select three horizontal lines to open the browser menu.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9741caf21803001222c1ad?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to save webpage as a pdf on Windows 5\" height=\"768\" width=\"1368\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The icon for the Firefox menu looks like a hamburger.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abbey White/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>3.</strong> From the dropdown menu, choose \"Print.\"</p><p><strong>4.</strong> The Print settings window will appear. Select \"Microsoft Print to PDF\" from the list of printer options.</p><ul><li>Note: Firefox doesn't include a built-in PDF printer, so you may need to use an extension if Microsoft Print isn't appearing.</li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f97421bf21803001222c1b0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"How to save webpage as PDF on Windows 7\" height=\"768\" width=\"1366\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You will need to print through Microsoft&#39;s PDF printer as the browser has no built-in option.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abbey White/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>5.</strong> Select \"Print.\"&#160;</p><p><strong>6.</strong> Name the file, select the file destination, and then click \"Save.\"&#160;</p><h2>Related coverage from&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">Tech Reference</a>:</h2><ul><li><h3><a
